## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (batch reactor ODE models)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of a species concentration A, which is the standard setup for chemical kinetics in a well-mixed (lumped) system. With only (t, A) available, the most likely relationships are rate laws dA_dt = f(A) possibly with explicit time-dependence capturing changing conditions (e.g., catalyst deactivation, ramps, forcing).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (rate independent of A; constant depletion until A is exhausted)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay; exponential concentration relaxation)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular/self-reaction; faster drop at high A)
- n-th order power-law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (general empirical/elementary rate order)
- Approach to equilibrium (linear driving force): dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (relaxation toward equilibrium concentration c1)
- Parallel pathways (mixed orders): dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (simultaneous first- and second-order loss channels)
- Autocatalytic/logistic-type kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (self-amplification with limiting term; can model autocatalysis with depletion/competition)
- Inhibited/saturating effective rate: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A) (effective first-order at low A with inhibition/saturation at high A)
- General rational rate law: dA_dt = -(c0 * A + c1 * A**2) / (1 + c2 * A) (captures saturation/inhibition and mixed-loss mechanisms)
- Time-ramped rate coefficient: dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (changing conditions over time, e.g., temperature program without explicitly modeling T)
- Catalyst deactivation / fading activity: dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (rate slows over time due to activity loss)
- Periodic forcing of rate: dA_dt = -c0 * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * A (externally driven modulation such as light/flow oscillations)
- Induction/lag effect (time-gated kinetics): dA_dt = -c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * t)) * A (rate turns on gradually after startup/mixing)
- Diffusion-controlled / fractional-order-like: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (0 < c1 < 1) (sub-linear dependence sometimes used for transport-limited regimes)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt is proportional to A (linear in A), A(t) tends to exhibit exponential decay/relaxation behavior.
- If dA_dt is approximately constant (independent of A), A(t) decreases roughly linearly in time until near depletion.
- Higher reaction order (e.g., A**2 or A**n with n>1) produces strong sensitivity to initial concentration: fast early decay then slowing as A drops.
- A term of the form -(A - c) indicates relaxation toward a nonzero steady-state concentration (equilibrium or reservoir-limited behavior).
- Sums of multiple loss terms (e.g., -A - A**2) suggest parallel/competing pathways with different mechanistic orders.
- A rational form A/(1 + c*A) indicates inhibition or saturation: near-first-order at low A, reduced incremental rate at high A.
- Explicit time factors multiplying A (e.g., exp(±c*t)*A) indicate changing operating conditions or catalyst activity varying with time.
- Sin(c*t) modulation suggests periodic external driving; it typically imprints oscillations in the instantaneous rate even if A remains monotone.
- Positive low-order growth with higher-order negative feedback (c*A - c*A**2) is a signature of autocatalysis/self-activation with limiting depletion.
